ASIANS FOOD 


ASIAN - FILIPINO MAIN DISHES
1. Adobo (chicken or pork) - is one of the most popular Filipino dishes. It is cooked by simmering meat in soy sauce, vinegar, garlic, and spices until flavorful and tender. 
	Ingredients
	* Chicken or pork
* Soy sauce
* Vinegar
* Garlic
* Bay leaves
* Pepper
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Marinate the meat in soy sauce and garlic.
2. Cook the meat in a pan.
3. Add vinegar, water, bay leaves, and pepper.
4. Simmer until the meat becomes tender.
5. Serve with rice.


	


2. Sinigang - is a classic Filipino dish known for its sour, savory broth—usually made with tamarind and a mix of meats and vegetables. Here are the typical ingredients: 
	Ingredients 
	* Pork, shrimp, or fish
* Tomatoes
* Onion
* Eggplant
* Okra
* String beans
* Water Spinach
* Radish
* Sinigang/Gabi mix
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Boil water with tomatoes and onion.
2. Add the meat or seafood.
3. Put the sinigang mix for sour flavor.
4. Add vegetables and cook until soft.
5. Serve hot.


	



3. Kare-Kare - is a traditional Filipino stew made with peanut sauce, vegetables, and meat. It is usually served with bagoong.
	Ingredients
	* Oxtail or beef
* Peanut butter
*  Eggplant
* String beans
* Banana blossom
* Garlic
* Onion
* Water
	Procedure
	1. Boil the meat until tender.
2. Sauté garlic and onion.
3.  Add peanut butter and water.
4. Put the cooked meat into the sauce.
5. Add the vegetables and cook until tender.
6. Serve with bagoong and rice.


	



4. Menudo - is a Filipino pork stew cooked with tomato sauce, vegetables, and liver.
	Ingredients
	* Pork
* Liver
* Tomato sauce
* Potatoes
* Carrots
* Garlic
* Onion
* Soy sauce


	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic and onion in a pan.
2. Add pork and cook until brown.
3. Add tomato sauce and soy sauce.
4. Put potatoes and carrots.
5. Simmer until the meat becomes tender.
6. Add liver and cook for a few minutes.
7. Serve hot with rice.


	



5. Caldereta - is a rich Filipino meat stew cooked with tomato sauce, vegetables, and spices.
	Ingredients
	* Beef or goat meat
* Tomato sauce
* Potatoes
* Carrots
* Bell peppers
* Garlic
* Onion
* Liver spread


	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic and onion.
2. Add the meat and cook until brown.
3. Pour tomato sauce and water.
4. Simmer until the meat is tender.
5. Add vegetables and liver spread.
6. Cook for a few more minutes.
7. Serve with rice.


	



6. Tinola - is a comforting Filipino chicken soup flavored with ginger and vegetables.        


	Ingredients
	* Chicken
* Ginger
* Garlic
* Onion
* Green papaya
* Chili leaves
* Water
* Fish sauce
	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic, onion, and ginger.
2. Add chicken and cook lightly.
3. Pour water and let it boil.
4. Simmer until the chicken becomes tender.
5. Add green papaya and chili leaves.
6. Season with fish sauce.
7. Serve hot.


	



7. Bicol Express - a spicy, creamy stew made from pork pieces cooked in coconut milk and a heavy amount of chili peppers.
	Ingredients
	* Pork belly cut into small cubes
* Serrano peppers or bird's eye chilies (sili)
* Coconut milk
* Coconut cream
* Shrimp paste (bagoong)
* Garlic and onion
* Ginger
	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic, onion, and ginger in a pan.
2. Add the shrimp paste and cook for a minute.
3. Add the pork cubes and cook until they turn light brown.
4. Pour in the coconut milk and bring to a simmer.
5. Add the chopped chilies and let it cook down until the pork is tender.
6. Pour in the coconut cream to thicken the sauce and render oil.
7. Serve hot with plenty of rice.
	



8. Beef Mechado - a tomato-based beef stew with potatoes, carrots, and bell peppers, traditionally larded with pork fat. 
	Ingredients
	* Beef chuck or stew meat
* Tomato sauce
* Soy sauce
* Calamansi juice or lemon juice
* Onions and garlic
* Potatoes
* Carrots
* Bell peppers
* Beef broth or water


	Procedure
	1. Marinate beef in soy sauce and calamansi juice for 30 minutes.
2. Sauté garlic and onions, then add the beef and sear.
3. Pour in the tomato sauce, marinade, and beef broth, then bring to a boil.
4. Simmer until the beef becomes tender.
5. Add the potatoes and carrots, cooking until soft.
6. Toss in the bell peppers and simmer for another 2 minutes.
7. Serve hot.


	



9. Dinuguan - a savory, dark Filipino stew made of pork offal or meat simmered in a rich, spicy pig's blood broth. 
	Ingredients
	* Pork meat and belly pieces
* Pig's blood
* Vinegar
* Long green chilies (sili haba)
* Garlic, onion, and ginger
* Beef or pork broth
* Fish sauce


	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic, onion, and ginger in a pot.
2. Add the pork pieces and cook until lightly browned.
3. Pour in fish sauce and a bit of broth, then simmer until the pork is tender. 
4. Add vinegar and let it boil without stirring.
5. Slowly pour in the pig's blood while stirring constantly to prevent clumping.
6. Add green chilies and simmer until the sauce thickens.
7. Serve hot, ideally with puto (steamed rice cakes).


	



10 Pinakbet - a traditional vegetable dish from northern Philippines flavored with fermented shrimp paste. 
	Ingredients
	* Pork belly (optional, for flavor)
* Shrimp paste (bagoong alamang)
* Bitter melon (ampalaya)
* Eggplant
* Okra
* String beans
* Squash (kalabasa)
* Tomatoes, garlic, and onion
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic, onion, and tomatoes in a pot.
2. Add pork belly and cook until fat renders.
3. Stir in the shrimp paste and cook for 2 minutes.
4. Add water and bring to a boil, then throw in the squash first until slightly soft.
5. Add the remaining vegetables (bitter melon, eggplant, okra, string beans).
6. Cover and simmer until all vegetables are tender but still crisp.
7. Serve hot.


	

FILIPINO DESSERTS




1. Halo-Halo - a famous layered dessert composed of shaved ice, evaporated milk, and various sweet ingredients. 
	Ingredients
	* Shaved ice
* Evaporated milk
* Sweetened beans, chickpeas, and nata de coco
* Leche flan (caramel custard)
* Ube halaya (purple yam jam)
* Ripe jackfruit (langka)
* Leche flan and Ube ice cream (for topping)
	Procedure
	1. In a tall glass, layer the sweetened fruits, beans, and jellies at the bottom.
2. Fill the glass with shaved ice.
3. Pour evaporated milk generously over the ice.
4. Top with a slice of leche flan, a dollop of ube halaya, and a scoop of ube ice cream.
5. Serve immediately with a long spoon to mix everything together.


	



2. Leche Flan - a rich, creamy caramel custard dessert topped with a golden sugar syrup. 
	Ingredients
	* Egg yolks
* Condensed milk
* Evaporated milk
* Sugar (for caramelizing)
* Vanilla extract


	Procedure
	1. Place sugar directly into aluminum molds (llaneras) and heat over a low flame until it melts into a golden caramel. Let it cool.
2. In a bowl, gently blend the egg yolks, condensed milk, evaporated milk, and vanilla extract without creating too many bubbles.
3. Strain the mixture through a fine mesh cloth into the caramelized molds.
4. Cover the molds tightly with aluminum foil.
5. Steam for about 30 to 35 minutes until the custard sets.
6. Let it cool, refrigerate, then flip onto a plate to serve.


	



3. Maja Blanca - a smooth, sweet coconut pudding made with cornstarch and studded with sweet corn kernels. 
	Ingredients
	* Coconut milk
* Condensed milk
* Evaporated milk
* Whole corn kernels
* Cornstarch
* Sugar
* Toasted grated coconut or latik (for topping)
	Procedure
	1. Combine coconut milk, condensed milk, evaporated milk, sugar, and sweet corn in a pot over medium heat.
2. Dissolve cornstarch in a small portion of water or milk, then stir it into the pot.
3. Stir continuously until the mixture thickens into a heavy paste.
4. Pour the hot mixture into a greased serving dish and smooth out the top.
5. Let it cool down and chill in the refrigerator until completely firm.
6. Garnish with latik or toasted coconut before slicing and serving.


	



4. Turon - sweet, crunchy deep-fried banana rolls wrapped in lumpia wrappers and coated with caramelized sugar. 
	Ingredients
	* Saba bananas (sliced lengthwise)
* Sweetened jackfruit strips (langka)
* Brown sugar
* Spring roll (lumpia) wrappers
* Cooking oil


	Procedure
	1. Roll each banana slice generously in brown sugar.
2. Place a sugar-coated banana slice and a strip of jackfruit onto a spring roll wrapper.
3. Fold the sides in and roll tightly, securing the edge with a dab of water.
4. Heat oil in a pan and sprinkle a few tablespoons of brown sugar directly into the hot oil.
5. Fry the wrapped bananas, rolling them in the melting caramel until the wrapper is crispy and glazed.
6. Drain excess oil and serve warm.


	



5. Cassava Cake - a moist, baked Filipino delicacy made from grated cassava, coconut milk, and a sweet custard topping. 
	Ingredients
	* Grated cassava
* Coconut milk
* Condensed milk
* Evaporated milk
* Sugar
* Eggs
* Cheddar cheese (grated, for topping)


	Procedure
	1. Combine grated cassava, coconut milk, condensed milk, evaporated milk, sugar, and egg whites in a large bowl.
2. Pour the mixture into a greased baking pan.
3. Bake in a preheated oven at 180°C (350°F) for about 45 minutes until almost firm.
4. Prepare the topping by mixing condensed milk, coconut milk, and egg yolks.
5. Pour the topping over the cake, sprinkle with grated cheese, and bake for another 15 minutes until golden brown.
6. Cool completely before slicing.


	



6. Buko Pandan - a refreshing, aromatic dessert made of pandan-flavored jelly cubes and shredded young coconut in sweet cream. 
	Ingredients
	* Shredded young coconut (buko)
* Pandan-flavored gelatin cubes
* All-purpose cream
* Condensed milk
* Tapioca pearls (sago)


	Procedure
	1. Prepare the pandan gelatin according to package instructions, let it set, and cut into cubes.
2. In a large mixing bowl, combine the all-purpose cream and condensed milk.
3. Add the shredded young coconut, gelatin cubes, and cooked tapioca pearls.
4. Mix thoroughly until well incorporated.
5. Chill in the refrigerator for at least 4 hours or overnight.
6. Serve chilled.


	



7. Puto - soft, fluffy Filipino steamed rice cakes often enjoyed as a snack or dessert, usually paired with savory dishes. 
	Ingredients
	* All-purpose flour or rice flour
* Baking powder
* Sugar
* Water or milk
* Melted butter
* Slices of cheese (for topping)


	Procedure
	1. Sift flour, baking powder, and sugar together in a bowl.
2. Gradually stir in the water or milk and melted butter until smooth.
3. Pour the batter into small greased molds until 3/4 full.
4. Arrange the molds in a steamer.
5. Steam for about 10 minutes, then place a small piece of cheese on top of each cake.
6. Steam for another 2 minutes until the cheese melts.
7. Remove from molds and serve warm.


	



8. Champorado - a comforting, sweet chocolate rice porridge made with glutinous rice and traditional tablea chocolate. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice (malagkit)
* Cocoa powder or Filipino chocolate tablea
* Sugar
* Water
* Evaporated milk or condensed milk (for serving)
* Fried dried fish (tuyo, optional for contrast)


	Procedure
	1. Boil water in a pot and add the glutinous rice.
2. Lower the heat and let the rice simmer, stirring occasionally to prevent sticking, until soft.
3. Dissolve the chocolate tablea or cocoa powder into the rice mixture.
4. Add sugar to taste and stir until fully dissolved and the mixture thickens.
5. Ladle into bowls.
6. Drizzle with evaporated or condensed milk before serving.


	



9. Kutsinta - a chewy, gelatinous steamed rice cake with a distinct reddish-brown color, served with grated coconut. 
	Ingredients
	* All-purpose flour
* Rice flour
* Brown sugar
* Lye water
* Water
* Annatto water (for color)
* Grated fresh coconut (for topping)


	Procedure
	1. In a bowl, mix all-purpose flour, rice flour, and brown sugar.
2. Gradually whisk in water and annatto water until free of lumps.
3. Add the lye water and blend thoroughly.
4. Strain the mixture into greased molds.
5. Steam for 40 to 45 minutes until the cakes become translucent and set.
6. Allow to cool completely before removing from the molds.
7. Serve topped with fresh grated coconut.


	



10. Banana Cue - deep-fried skewered saba bananas heavily coated with caramelized brown sugar. 
	Ingredients
	* Saba bananas
* Brown sugar
* Cooking oil
* Bamboo skewers


	Procedure
	1. Heat oil in a large pan over medium heat.
2. Add the brown sugar directly into the hot oil and let it melt and float.
3. Add the bananas into the pan and fry them.
4. Adjust the heat and turn the bananas continuously so the melting sugar coats them evenly.
5. Once the bananas are cooked through and fully glazed, remove them from the oil.
6. Skew two to three bananas onto each bamboo stick.
7. Allow to cool slightly so the sugar hardens before serving.


	

FILIPINO BEVERAGES


1. Sago’t Gulaman - a classic, sweet, and icy Filipino beverage featuring tapioca pearls and gelatin cubes in a brown sugar syrup. 
	Ingredients
	* Cooked tapioca pearls (sago)
* Gelatin cubes (gulaman)
* Brown sugar
* Water
* Vanilla extract or pandan essence
* Crushed ice


	Procedure
	1. Boil brown sugar and water together to create a thick sugar syrup (arnibal).
2. Remove from heat and add a drop of vanilla extract for aroma, then let it cool.
3. In a large pitcher, combine water, the prepared sugar syrup, and stir well.
4. Add the cooked tapioca pearls and gelatin cubes.
5. Add crushed ice into glasses.
6. Pour the mixture over the ice and serve cold.


	



2. Buko Juice - a naturally sweet and refreshing drink made from fresh young coconut water and tender coconut meat strips. 
	Ingredients
	* Fresh young coconut water
* Shredded young coconut meat
* Sugar or condensed milk (optional, to sweeten)
* Ice cubes


	Procedure
	1. Crack open a fresh young coconut and pour the water into a pitcher.
2. Scrape out the soft coconut meat using a shredder or spoon and add it to the water.
3. Taste the juice and stir in sugar or a touch of condensed milk if you prefer it sweeter.
4. Mix thoroughly until the sweetener dissolves.
5. Add ice cubes to chill.
6. Serve chilled in glasses.


	



3. Calamansi Juice - a refreshing citrus drink made from fresh calamansi lime juice, water, and sweetener. 
	Ingredients
	* Fresh calamansi fruits
* Water
* Sugar or honey
* Ice cubes


	Procedure
	1. Slice the top off the calamansi fruits.
2. Squeeze the juice through a fine strainer into a pitcher to catch the seeds.
3. Add water to dilute the strong sour taste.
4. Stir in sugar or honey according to your preferred sweetness.
5. Mix well until the sweetener completely dissolves.
6. Add ice cubes and serve ice-cold.


	



Melon Juice - a sweet, refreshing summer drink made from shredded cantaloupe melon mixed with water and sugar. 
	Ingredients
	* Cantaloupe melon
* Water
* Sugar
* Evaporated milk (optional, for a creamy version)
* Ice cubes


	Procedure
	1. Slice the melon in half, scrape out the seeds, and discard them.
2. Use a melon scraper to shred the melon flesh into thin strands.
3. Place the shredded melon and its natural juices into a pitcher.
4. Add water and sugar, stirring until the sugar dissolves.
5. Pour in a splash of evaporated milk if you want a creamy texture.
6. Serve cold over ice.


	



5. Kapeng Barako - a bold, strong, and highly aromatic black coffee brewed from Liberica coffee beans grown in Batangas. 
	Ingredients
	* Ground Barako coffee beans
* Water
* Brown sugar or honey (optional)


	Procedure
	1. Boil water in a pot or coffee maker.
2. Add the ground Barako coffee beans directly to the boiling water if using the traditional boiling method.
3. Let it simmer on low heat for about 3 to 5 minutes to extract the full flavor.
4. Turn off the heat and let the coffee grounds settle at the bottom of the pot.
5. Strain the coffee liquid into a cup.
6. Serve hot as black coffee, or stir in brown sugar to taste.


	











ASIAN - KOREAN MAIN DISHES


1. Kimchi Jjigae - a comforting, spicy Korean stew made with well-fermented kimchi, pork, and tofu. 
	Ingredients
	* Aged kimchi (sliced)
* Pork belly or pork shoulder
* Tofu (sliced)
* Green onions
* Garlic
* Gochugaru (Korean chili flakes)
* Gochujang (Korean chili paste)
* Water or kelp broth


	Procedure
	1. Sauté the pork and garlic in a pot until the pork is lightly browned.
2. Add the aged kimchi and stir-fry with the pork for a few minutes.
3. Pour in the water or kelp broth and bring to a boil.
4. Stir in the gochugaru and gochujang, then lower the heat to a simmer.
5. Let it simmer until the kimchi becomes very soft and tender.
6. Add the tofu slices and green onions, cooking for another 5 minutes.
7. Serve bubbling hot with steamed rice.


	



2. Bulgogi - thinly sliced beef marinated in a sweet and savory sauce, then grilled or stir-fried. 
	Ingredients
	* Thinly sliced beef (ribeye or sirloin)
* Soy sauce
* Brown sugar
* Grated Asian pear (for tenderizing)
* Minced garlic and ginger
* Sesame oil
* Green onions
* Toasted sesame seeds


	Procedure
	1. Mix soy sauce, sugar, grated pear, garlic, ginger, and sesame oil in a bowl.
2. Add the beef slices to the marinade, mixing well to coat each piece.
3. Marinate in the refrigerator for at least 30 minutes.
4. Heat a pan or grill over high heat.
5. Stir-fry the beef quickly along with chopped green onions until cooked through.
6. Garnish with toasted sesame seeds.
7. Serve hot, optionally wrapped in lettuce leaves.


	



3. Bibimbap - a colorful bowl of warm rice topped with an array of seasoned vegetables, meat, and a fried egg. 
	Ingredients
	* Cooked short-grain rice
* Ground beef or sliced beef
* Spinach, bean sprouts, carrots, and shiitake mushrooms
* Eggs
* Soy sauce and garlic
* Gochujang (Korean chili paste)
* Sesame oil and sesame seeds


	Procedure
	* Sauté each vegetable separately with a bit of garlic, sesame oil, and salt.
* Cook the beef in a pan with soy sauce and garlic until browned.
* Fry an egg, keeping the yolk runny.
* Place a generous scoop of warm rice at the bottom of a bowl.
* Arrange the seasoned vegetables and meat neatly in sections on top of the rice.
* Place the fried egg in the center.
* Serve with a dollop of gochujang and a drizzle of sesame oil to mix before eating.


	



4. Tteokbokki - a highly popular street food consisting of chewy rice cakes cooked in a spicy, sweet chili sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Korean rice cakes (tteok)
* Korean fish cakes (eomuk)
* Gochujang (Korean chili paste)
* Gochugaru (Korean chili flakes)
* Sugar or corn syrup
* Soy sauce and minced garlic
* Anchovy and kelp broth
* Green onions


	Procedure
	* Bring the anchovy and kelp broth to a boil in a shallow pan.
* Whisk in the gochujang, gochugaru, sugar, soy sauce, and garlic until dissolved.
* Add the rice cakes and sliced fish cakes into the boiling sauce.
* Reduce heat to medium and stir continuously so the rice cakes don't stick.
* Simmer until the sauce thickens and the rice cakes become soft and chewy.
* Toss in the chopped green onions during the last minute.
* Serve hot.


	



5. Samgyetang - a nourishing, traditional chicken soup stuffed with ginseng, garlic, and glutinous rice. 
	Ingredients
	* Whole young chicken
* Glutinous rice (soaked)
* Fresh ginseng root
* Dried jujubes (red dates)
* Garlic cloves
* Ginger slices
* Water
* Green onions, salt, and black pepper


	Procedure
	1. Wash the chicken thoroughly and stuff the cavity with the soaked glutinous rice, garlic cloves, and ginseng.
2. Cross the chicken's legs and tie them to keep the stuffing inside.
3. Place the stuffed chicken in a large pot with water, jujubes, and ginger.
4. Bring to a boil over high heat, skimming off any foam that rises.
5. Cover, reduce heat to medium-low, and simmer for about an hour until the chicken is tender.
6. Garnish with plenty of chopped green onions.
7. Serve hot with salt and pepper on the side for dipping.


	



6. Jajangmyeon - thick wheat noodles topped with a rich, dark sauce made from sweet black bean paste and diced pork. 
	Ingredients
	* Jajangmyeon noodles (thick wheat noodles)
* Korean black bean paste (chunjang)
* Pork belly or pork shoulder (diced)
* Zucchini, cabbage, and onions (diced)
* Sugar and soy sauce
* Potato starch slurry (for thickening)
* Cooking oil and water


	Procedure
	1. Fry the black bean paste in a bit of oil for a few minutes to remove bitterness, then set aside.
2. In a pan, stir-fry the pork until cooked, then add onions, cabbage, and zucchini.
3. Stir the fried black bean paste into the meat and vegetables.
4. Pour in water, add sugar, and bring to a simmer until the vegetables are soft.
5. Pour in the starch slurry to thicken the dark sauce.
6. Boil the noodles in a separate pot, drain, and place in a serving bowl.
7. Ladle the hot black bean sauce over the noodles and serve immediately.


	



7. Galbitang - a clear, hearty soup made by simmering beef short ribs for hours alongside radish and herbs. 
	Ingredients
	* Beef short ribs (galbi)
* Korean radish (mu)
* Garlic cloves and onion
* Soy sauce (for soup)
* Salt and black pepper
* Dangmyeon (sweet potato starch noodles, soaked)
* Green onions
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Soak the short ribs in cold water for an hour to extract excess blood, then parboil and rinse.
2. Place the cleaned ribs in a large pot with fresh water, onion, and garlic, then bring to a boil.
3. Lower the heat and simmer for an hour, adding the radish chunks halfway through.
4. Remove the onion and garlic, and slice the cooked radish into bite-sized pieces.
5. Season the clear broth with soup soy sauce, salt, and pepper.
6. Add the soaked starch noodles to the bowl and ladle the boiling soup and ribs over them.
7. Top with chopped green onions and serve.


	



8. Sundubu Jjigae - a fiery, silky soft tofu stew cooked with seafood or pork in a spicy broth, finished with a raw egg. 
	Ingredients
	* Soft/silken tofu (sundubu)
* Mixed seafood (shrimp, clams, squid) or pork
* Gochugaru (Korean chili flakes)
* Garlic and green onions
* Sesame oil
* Anchovy broth or water
* Fish sauce or salt
* Raw egg


	Procedure
	1. Sauté garlic and gochugaru in sesame oil over low heat to create a chili oil base.
2. Add the seafood or pork and stir-fry quickly.
3. Pour in the anchovy broth and bring to a boil.
4. Scoop the silken tofu into the pot in large chunks.
5. Season the soup with fish sauce or salt to taste.
6. Add green onions and let it boil for 3 minutes.
7. Crack a raw egg directly into the boiling stew right before serving.
	



9. Japchae - a sweet and savory stir-fried dish made of glass noodles, mixed vegetables, and strips of beef. 
	Ingredients
	* Dangmyeon (sweet potato starch glass noodles)
* Beef strips
* Spinach, carrots, onions, and shiitake mushrooms
* Soy sauce
* Sugar
* Garlic
* Sesame oil and toasted sesame seeds


	Procedure
	1. Boil the glass noodles until chewy, drain, and toss with a little soy sauce and sesame oil.
2. Blanch the spinach, squeeze dry, and season with salt and sesame oil.
3. Stir-fry the carrots, onions, and mushrooms separately with a pinch of salt.
4. Cook the beef strips with soy sauce, sugar, and garlic.
5. In a large mixing bowl, combine the noodles, vegetables, and beef together.
6. Pour in a mixture of soy sauce, sugar, and sesame oil, tossing everything gently by hand.
7. Garnish with sesame seeds and serve warm or at room temperature.
	





10. Dakgalbi - a spicy, flavor-packed stir-fried chicken dish cooked with cabbage, sweet potatoes, and rice cakes on a hot plate. 
	Ingredients
	* Boneless chicken thighs (cut into bite-sized pieces)
* Cabbage (chopped)
* Korean sweet potato (sliced)
* Rice cakes (tteok)
* Gochujang, gochugaru, soy sauce, and sugar
* Minced garlic and ginger
* Green onions and perilla leaves


	Procedure
	1. Make a marinade by mixing gochujang, gochugaru, soy sauce, sugar, garlic, and ginger.
2. Coat the chicken pieces in the marinade and rest for 30 minutes.
3. Heat a large skillet or skillet pan with a little oil.
4. Add the marinated chicken, sweet potatoes, cabbage, and rice cakes.
5. Stir-fry over medium-high heat until the chicken and sweet potatoes are fully cooked.
6. Toss in green onions and perilla leaves at the end.
7. Serve directly from the skillet.
	



KOREAN - DESSERTS


1. Patbingsu - a widely popular shaved ice dessert topped with sweet red beans, rice cakes, and condensed milk. 
	Ingredients
	* Shaved ice (or frozen milk ice)
* Sweetened red bean paste (pat)
* Tteok (mini rice cake cubes)
* Condensed milk
* Misugaru (roasted grain powder, optional)


	Procedure
	1. Shave frozen milk or regular ice into a serving bowl.
2. Spoon a generous amount of sweetened red bean paste directly onto the center of the ice.
3. Drizzle condensed milk evenly over the shaved ice.
4. Scatter chewy mini rice cakes around the red bean paste.
5. Dust with misugaru powder if desired.
6. Serve immediately.
	



2. Hotteok - sweet, pan-fried Korean pancakes stuffed with a gooey filling of brown sugar, cinnamon, and nuts. 
	Ingredients
	* Yeast dough (wheat flour, water, milk, yeast, sugar)
* Dark brown sugar
* Cinnamon powder
* Chopped walnuts or sunflower seeds
* Cooking oil


	Procedure
	1. Let the yeast dough rise until it doubles in size.
2. Mix brown sugar, cinnamon, and chopped nuts together in a small bowl for the filling.
3. Take a piece of dough, flatten it in your hand, and place a spoonful of filling in the center.
4. Seal the dough tightly around the filling to form a ball.
5. Place the ball into a hot, oiled pan and press it flat with a presser or spatula.
6. Fry until golden brown on both sides, making sure the sugar inside melts into a syrup.
7. Serve warm.


	



3. Yakgwa - a traditional, deep-fried Korean pastry made from wheat flour and oil, then soaked in a sweet ginger syrup. 
	Ingredients
	* Wheat flour
* Sesame oil
* Honey or rice syrup
* Ginger juice or minced ginger
* Water and a pinch of salt
* Cooking oil for frying


	Procedure
	1. Rub sesame oil into the wheat flour until well incorporated, then sift.
2. Mix honey, water, ginger juice, and salt, then gently knead into the flour to form a dough.
3. Roll out the dough and cut it into traditional flower shapes or squares.
4. Deep-fry the pastry shapes in low-temperature oil first, then increase the heat to brown them.
5. Drain the fried pastries and submerge them in a warm honey-ginger syrup for several hours.
6. Remove from syrup, drain excess, and let them set before serving.


	



4. Gyeongdan - sweet, chewy rice cake balls made from glutinous rice flour and coated in various colorful powders. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice flour
* Hot water
* Salt
* Fillings (optional, like sweet red bean paste)
* Coatings (black sesame powder, roasted soybean powder, mugwort powder)


	Procedure
	1. Mix glutinous rice flour with hot water and a pinch of salt to form a smooth dough.
2. Roll the dough into bite-sized balls (stuffed with red bean paste if preferred).
3. Drop the balls into boiling water and cook until they float to the surface.
4. Transfer the cooked balls into an ice bath to cool down and become chewy.
5. Drain the water completely.
6. Roll the balls in your choice of roasted soybean powder or black sesame powder until coated.
7. Serve at room temperature.


	



5. Bungeoppang - a famous fish-shaped pastry crust filled with sweet red bean paste, crispy on the outside and soft inside. 
	Ingredients
	* Pastry batter (flour, baking powder, sugar, milk, water, egg)
* Sweetened red bean paste
* Melted butter or oil (for greasing)
	Procedure
	1. Preheat a fish-shaped waffle mold iron over the stove.
2. Brush the molds lightly with melted butter or oil.
3. Pour a thin layer of batter into each fish mold.
4. Add a scoop of sweet red bean paste into the center of the batter.
5. Pour more batter over the red bean paste to cover it completely.
6. Close the mold and cook over low-medium heat, flipping occasionally, until both sides are golden brown.
7. Remove carefully and serve warm.
	



6. Songpyeon - half-moon-shaped rice cakes traditionally prepared during Chuseok, steamed over a bed of fresh pine needles. 
	Ingredients
	* Rice flour (non-glutinous)
* Hot water
* Fillings (toasted sesame seeds with honey, sweet red bean, or chestnuts)
* Fresh pine needles
* Sesame oil
	Procedure
	1. Knead the rice flour with hot water until a smooth, pliable dough forms.
2. Take small pieces of dough, shape into a small bowl, and add your preferred sweet filling.
3. Fold and pinch the edges tightly to form a signature half-moon shape.
4. Line a steamer tray with clean, fresh pine needles.
5. Arrange the rice cakes on top and steam for about 20 minutes.
6. Rinse the steamed cakes quickly in cold water, remove stray needles, and brush lightly with sesame oil.
7. Serve cool.


	



7. Hwajeon - delicate, small pan-fried sweet rice cakes garnished with beautiful, edible fresh flower petals. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice flour
* Hot water
* Edible flowers (such as azaleas, chrysanthemums, or rose petals)
* Honey or sugar syrup
* Cooking oil


	Procedure
	1. Knead glutinous rice flour with hot water and a touch of salt into a soft dough.
2. Divide the dough into small pieces and flatten them into small, round discs.
3. Gently rinse and dry the edible flower petals.
4. Heat a pan with oil over low heat and pan-fry the rice discs.
5. Carefully press an edible flower petal onto the top side of each disc while cooking.
6. Flip briefly to set the flower, being careful not to burn it.
7. Remove from heat, drizzle with honey or sugar syrup, and serve.


	



8. Sikhye Granita - a modern icy twist on the traditional sweet rice drink, frozen and scraped into a refreshing dessert slush. 
	Ingredients
	* Traditional Sikhye (sweet rice beverage)
* Pine nuts (for garnish)


	Procedure
	1. Pour sweet sikhye beverage (including some rice grains) into a shallow baking dish.
2. Place the dish flat in the freezer for about 2 hours.
3. Take the dish out and use a fork to thoroughly scrape the frozen parts into ice crystals.
4. Return to the freezer and repeat the scraping process every hour until it reaches a uniform slush texture.
5. Scoop the icy granita into a dessert bowl.
6. Garnish with a few pine nuts on top and serve cold.


	



9. Chapssaltteok - a soft, chewy Korean rice cake made from glutinous rice and stuffed heavily with sweet red bean paste. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice flour
* Sugar and salt
* Water
* Sweetened red bean paste
* Cornstarch or potato starch (for dusting)


	Procedure
	1. Mix glutinous rice flour, sugar, salt, and water in a microwave-safe bowl.
2. Cover and microwave for 2 minutes, stir, then microwave for another 1 minute until sticky and translucent.
3. Pound the hot dough briefly with a wooden spoon to increase chewiness.
4. Dust a clean surface generously with cornstarch and roll out the dough.
5. Cut into squares, place a ball of red bean paste in the center of each, and seal the edges.
6. Coat the outside lightly with starch so it isn't sticky.
7. Let cool and serve.


	



10. Mat-tang - deep-fried sweet potato chunks coated in a hard, crunchy, caramelized sugar glaze. 
	Ingredients
	* Korean sweet potatoes
* Cooking oil for deep frying
* Sugar
* Water
* Black sesame seeds


	Procedure
	1. Peel the sweet potatoes and cut them into bite-sized, irregular chunks.
2. Deep-fry the sweet potato chunks in hot oil until the inside is soft and the outside turns golden brown. Drain.
3. In a clean pan, combine sugar and water over medium heat without stirring until it melts into a golden syrup.
4. Quickly toss the fried sweet potatoes into the caramel syrup, coating each piece evenly.
5. Transfer the glazed chunks onto a greased plate, spacing them out so they don't stick together.
6. Sprinkle with black sesame seeds and let the glaze cool and harden before serving.


	

KOREAN - BEVERAGES 


1. Sikhye - a sweet, traditional Korean malt beverage containing grains of cooked rice and a distinct ginger-malt aroma 
	* Ingredients
	* Malted barley powder (yeotgireum)
* Water
* Cooked white rice
* Sugar
* Pine nuts (for garnish)


	Procedure
	1. Soak malted barley powder in warm water, stir, and strain the liquid, leaving the sediment behind.
2. Pour the clear malt water into a rice cooker over cooked white rice.
3. Keep the rice cooker on the "warm" setting for 4 to 5 hours until rice grains begin to float.
4. Pour the liquid and rice into a large pot, add sugar, and boil for 10 minutes.
5. Skim off any foam from the surface.
6. Chill thoroughly in the refrigerator.
7. Serve ice-cold, garnished with a few pine nuts.


	



2. Sujeonggwa - a dark, refreshing dessert punch made from boiled cinnamon and ginger, sweetened and served cold. 
	Ingredients
	* Cinnamon sticks
* Fresh ginger slices
* Water
* Brown sugar or white sugar
* Dried persimmons (gotgam)
* Pine nuts


	Procedure
	1. Boil ginger and cinnamon sticks in separate pots of water to extract their individual flavors cleanly.
2. Strain both liquids into one large pot, discarding the ginger pieces and cinnamon sticks.
3. Add sugar and simmer for another 10 minutes until completely dissolved, then let the punch cool down.
4. Refrigerate the liquid until cold.
5. Slice dried persimmons and soak them in the punch shortly before serving so they soften.
6. Ladle into cups and garnish with a few pine nuts.


	



3. Yuja-cha - a sweet, citrusy tea made by mixing hot water with a marmalade-like preserved yuzu citrus fruit. 
	Ingredients
	* Yuja cheong (Korean yuzu marmalade/preserve)
* Hot water


	Procedure
	1. Scoop 2 to 3 tablespoons of yuja cheong into a teacup.
2. Pour hot water directly over the preserve.
3. Stir thoroughly until the sweet syrup blends completely with the water.
4. Let it steep for a minute so the citrus rinds release their flavor.
5. Serve hot (can also be served over ice for a cold option).


	



4. Boricha - a roasted barley tea with a rich, nutty flavor that is consumed daily in Korean households. 
	Ingredients
	* Roasted barley grains
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Bring a large pot of water to a rolling boil.
2. Add a handful of roasted barley grains directly into the boiling water.
3. Reduce the heat to low and let it simmer for about 15 to 20 minutes until the water turns a light amber color.
4. Turn off the heat and let it steep for another 10 minutes.
5. Strain out the barley grains.
6. Serve warm or transfer to a bottle and chill in the refrigerator to drink cold.


	



5. Misugaru Shake - a thick, nutritious beverage made of roasted mixed grain powder blended with milk and sweet honey. 
	Ingredients
	* Misugaru powder (roasted multi-grain powder)
* Milk or water
* Honey or sugar
* Ice cubes


	Procedure
	1. Add misugaru powder into a blender or shaker bottle.
2. Pour in cold milk or water.
3. Drizzle in honey or sugar to suit your preferred sweetness.
4. Blend or shake vigorously until the powder is fully dissolved and smooth with no lumps.
5. Pour into a glass filled with ice cubes.
6. Serve cold as a refreshing snack or breakfast drink.


	



JAPAN - MAIN COURSE
1. Chicken Katsu Curry - a comforting dish featuring a crispy, panko-breaded chicken cutlet served over rice with a rich curry sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Chicken breasts or thighs
* Panko (Japanese breadcrumbs)
* Flour and beaten eggs
* Japanese curry roux blocks
* Potatoes, carrots, and onions
* Cooking oil
* Water or dashi broth
* Steamed white rice


	Procedure
	1. Dredge chicken in flour, dip in beaten eggs, and coat thoroughly with panko.
2. Deep-fry the chicken cutlet until golden brown and crispy, then slice into strips.
3. In a separate pot, sauté sliced onions, carrots, and potatoes.
4. Add water or dashi broth and simmer until the vegetables are tender.
5. Turn off the heat, drop in the curry roux blocks, and stir until completely dissolved.
6. Simmer on low heat for a few minutes until the curry sauce thickens.
7. Plate a serving of rice, place the crispy chicken on top, and pour the hot curry sauce over it.


	



2. Tonkotsu Ramen - a rich, deeply savory noodle soup made from a creamy pork bone broth topped with tender pork slices. 
	Ingredients
	* Ramen noodles
* Pork bones (for the broth)
* Chashu (braised pork belly slices)
* Ajitsuke Tamago (marinated soft-boiled egg)
* Green onions
* Nori (dried seaweed sheets)
* Menma (seasoned bamboo shoots)
* Soy sauce and mirin (for the tare seasoning base)


	Procedure
	1. Boil pork bones in water for several hours until the marrow breaks down and the broth becomes milky and creamy.
2. Prepare the tare seasoning by simmering soy sauce, mirin, and a bit of garlic.
3. Boil the ramen noodles in a separate pot until al dente, then drain.
4. Place a spoonful of tare base at the bottom of a serving bowl.
5. Pour the boiling tonkotsu pork broth over the tare and stir.
6. Add the noodles and neatly arrange the chashu, soft-boiled egg, green onions, and nori on top.
7. Serve immediately while piping hot.
	



3. Gyudon - a popular, quick rice bowl topped with thinly sliced beef and tender onions simmered in a sweet dashi broth. 
	Ingredients
	* Thinly sliced beef (short plate or ribeye)
* Onions (sliced)
* Dashi broth
* Soy sauce
* Mirin
* Sugar
* Steamed white rice
* Pickled red ginger (beni shoga, for garnish)
	Procedure
	1. In a pan, combine dashi broth, soy sauce, mirin, and sugar, then bring to a boil.
2. Add the sliced onions and cook until they become soft and translucent.
3. Add the thinly sliced beef to the simmering liquid and cook quickly until no longer pink.
4. Skim off any foam or fat that floats to the surface.
5. Fill a bowl with warm, steamed rice.
6. Ladle the beef, onions, and a generous splash of the sweet savory broth over the rice.
7. Garnish with pickled red ginger and serve hot.


	



4. Chicken Teriyaki - tender pieces of pan-seared chicken glazed in a glossy, sweet, and savory soy-based sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Chicken thighs (skin-on preferred)
* Soy sauce
* Mirin
* Sake
* Sugar
* Grated ginger
* Cooking oil


	Procedure
	1. Mix soy sauce, mirin, sake, sugar, and grated ginger in a bowl to create the teriyaki sauce.
2. Heat oil in a pan and place the chicken skin-side down, cooking until the skin is crispy and golden.
3. Flip the chicken over and cook the other side until completely done.
4. Wipe away any excess rendered fat from the pan using a paper towel.
5. Pour the teriyaki sauce mixture into the pan with the chicken.
6. Simmer over medium heat, spooning the sauce over the chicken continuously until it reduces into a thick glaze.
7. Slice the chicken, drizzle with the remaining pan glaze, and serve.


	



5. Tempura - light and airy seafood and vegetables dipped in a cold batter and deep-fried to crispy perfection. 
	Ingredients
	* Large shrimp (peeled and straightened)
* Vegetables (sweet potato, eggplant, pumpkin, or shiitake mushrooms)
* Tempura flour
* Ice-cold water
* Egg yolk
* Oil for deep frying
* Tentsuyu (dipping sauce made from dashi, soy sauce, and mirin)


	Procedure
	1. Whisk the egg yolk and ice-cold water together, then gently mix in the tempura flour (leave lumps for maximum crispiness).
2. Heat a generous amount of oil in a deep pot to around 170°C to 180°C.
3. Dust the shrimp and vegetable slices lightly with dry flour.
4. Dip each piece into the cold tempura batter, ensuring a light coating.
5. Drop carefully into the hot oil and deep-fry for 2 to 3 minutes until pale gold and crispy.
6. Drain on a wire rack or paper towels.
7. Serve immediately accompanied by warm tentsuyu dipping sauce and grated radish.


	



6. Sukiyaki - a hot pot dish where sliced beef, tofu, and assorted vegetables are simmered at the table in a sweet soy sauce broth. 
	Ingredients
	* Thinly sliced beef
* Grilled tofu (yaki-dofu)
* Shiitake and enoki mushrooms
* Nagaogi (Japanese long green onion)
* Shirataki noodles
* Soy sauce, mirin, sake, and sugar (for the warishita broth)
* Fresh raw eggs (for dipping)


	Procedure
	1. Mix soy sauce, mirin, sake, and sugar in a pot and bring to a light boil to make the sukiyaki broth (warishita).
2. Heat a shallow hot pot pan and sear a few pieces of beef, then pour in a bit of the broth.
3. Arrange the tofu, mushrooms, green onions, and shirataki noodles neatly in separate sections of the pot.
4. Pour the remaining warishita broth over the ingredients and let it simmer until everything is cooked through.
5. Beat a raw egg in a small individual dipping bowl.
Take the cooked beef and vegetables directly from the pot, dip into the raw egg, and eat immediately.


	



7. Katsudon - a satisfying rice bowl topped with a deep-fried pork cutlet and sliced onions simmered in a sweet dashi egg mixture. 
	Ingredients
	* Tonkatsu (crispy deep-fried pork cutlet)
* Onion (sliced)
* Egg (lightly beaten)
* Dashi broth
* Soy sauce and mirin
* Sugar
* Steamed white rice


	Procedure
	1. Combine dashi, soy sauce, mirin, and sugar in a small skillet and bring to a simmer.
2. Add the sliced onions and cook until softened.
3. Slice the pre-cooked tonkatsu pork cutlet and place it directly on top of the simmering onions.
4. Drizzle the beaten egg evenly over the pork cutlet and onions.
5. Cover the skillet with a lid and cook on low heat for 1 to 2 minutes until the egg is softly set but still runny.
6. Slide the entire mixture carefully over a large bowl of warm rice.
7. Serve hot.


	



8. Oyakodon - a classic soul food rice bowl made by simmering chicken and onions in a dashi broth, bound together with a soft-cooked egg. 
	Ingredients
	* Chicken thigh (cut into bite-sized pieces)
* Onion (sliced)
* Eggs (lightly beaten)
* Dashi broth
* Soy sauce
* Mirin
* Sugar
* Steamed white rice


	Procedure
	1. Pour dashi broth, soy sauce, mirin, and sugar into a small pan and heat until simmering.
2. Add the chicken pieces and sliced onions, cooking until the chicken is tender and no longer pink.
3. Pour the beaten eggs in a circular motion over the chicken and onions.
4. Cover with a lid and let the egg cook for about 1 minute until it is partially set.
5. Turn off the heat while the egg is still glossy and soft.
6. Slide the chicken and egg smoothly over a bowl of warm rice.
7. Serve immediately.


	



9. Yakisoba - savory stir-fried wheat noodles cooked on a griddle with pork, cabbage, and a tangy barbecue-like sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Yakisoba noodles (steamed wheat noodles)
* Pork belly slices (cut into small pieces)
* Cabbage (chopped)
* Carrots and onions (sliced)
* Yakisoba sauce (sauce mix or Worcestershire mixed with oyster sauce and ketchup)
* Cooking oil
* Aonori (dried green seaweed powder) and pickled red ginger (for garnish)


	Procedure
	1. Heat oil in a large pan or griddle and stir-fry the pork belly until browned.
2. Add the onions, carrots, and cabbage, cooking until the vegetables are slightly wilted but still crisp.
3. Add the yakisoba noodles to the pan along with a splash of water to help loosen them up.
4. Stir-fry everything together until the noodles are well incorporated.
5. Pour the yakisoba sauce over the noodles and toss vigorously to coat evenly.
6. Transfer to a plate.
7. Garnish with a dusting of aonori and a side of pickled red ginger.


	



10. Saba Shioyaki - a simple yet delicious traditional dish of mackerel salted heavily and grilled until the skin is perfectly crispy. 
	Ingredients
	* Mackerel fillets (saba)
* Coarse sea salt
* Daikon radish (grated, for serving)
* Soy sauce (for serving)
* Cooking oil (for greasing the grill grate)


	Procedure
	1. Sprinkle a generous amount of coarse sea salt on both sides of the mackerel fillets and let sit for 20 minutes to draw out moisture.
2. Wipe the fillets completely dry with a paper towel and lightly salt them again.
3. Preheat a fish broiler, oven grill, or grill pan and oil the grate lightly.
4. Place the mackerel skin-side down and grill until the skin becomes crispy and blisters.
5. Flip the fillets over and grill the flesh side until cooked through and juicy.
6. Place on a serving plate alongside a mound of grated daikon radish.
7. Drizzle soy sauce over the radish and serve warm.


	

JAPAN - DESSERTS


1. Matcha Mochi - a soft, chewy sweet rice cake infused with Japanese green tea powder and filled with red bean paste. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice flour (shiratamako or mochiko)
* Matcha powder
* Sugar
* Water
* Sweet red bean paste (anko)
* Cornstarch (for dusting)


	Procedure
	1. In a microwave-safe bowl, whisk together the glutinous rice flour, matcha powder, sugar, and water until smooth.
2. Cover the bowl loosely and microwave for 2 minutes. Stir well, then microwave for another 1 minute until sticky.
3. Dust a clean surface generously with cornstarch and transfer the hot dough onto it.
4. Divide the dough into equal pieces and flatten them into small rounds.
5. Place a small ball of sweet red bean paste in the center of each round.
6. Pinch the edges of the mochi dough together to seal it completely.
7. Shape into smooth balls and serve at room temperature.


	



2. Dorayaki - a popular snack featuring a sweet red bean paste sandwiched between two fluffy, honey-infused pancakes. 
	Ingredients
	* Eggs
* Sugar
* Honey
* All-purpose flour
* Baking powder
* Water or milk
* Sweet red bean paste (anko)
* Vegetable oil


	Procedure
	1. Whisk eggs, sugar, and honey together until fluffy, then sift in the flour and baking powder.
2. Stir in water or milk to create a smooth, slightly thick pancake batter, then let it rest for 10 minutes.
3. Lightly oil a non-stick pan over low heat and wipe off excess oil completely.
4. Pour a small ladle of batter to form a small, neat circle.
5. Cook until bubbles appear on the surface, then flip and cook the other side for 1 minute. Repeat to make an even number of pancakes.
6. Let the pancakes cool down completely.
7. Spread a generous dollop of sweet red bean paste onto one pancake and sandwich it with another.


	



3. Matcha Soft Serve Ice Cream - a smooth, creamy frozen dessert with the distinctly earthy and bitter-sweet notes of green tea. 
	Ingredients
	* Heavy cream
* Whole milk
* Sugar
* High-quality matcha powder
* A pinch of salt


	Procedure
	1. Whisk the matcha powder and sugar together in a small bowl.
2. Gradually whisk in a small portion of warm milk until the matcha dissolves smoothly with no remaining lumps.
3. In a larger bowl, combine the matcha mixture, remaining milk, heavy cream, and a pinch of salt.
4. Stir thoroughly and chill the liquid mixture in the refrigerator for at least 2 hours.
5. Pour the chilled base into an ice cream maker and churn according to the manufacturer's directions until soft-serve consistency.
6. Scoop into a bowl or pipe into a waffle cone.
7. Serve immediately.


	



4. Castella Cake - a moist, dense sponge cake brought by Portuguese merchants but refined into a classic Japanese treat. 
	Ingredients
	* Eggs
* Bread flour (for a chewily dense texture)
* Sugar
* Honey
* Warm water
* 	Procedure
	1. Whisk honey and warm water together in a small bowl until dissolved.
2. Whip the eggs and sugar together using an electric mixer on high speed until thick, pale, and ribbon-like.
3. Add the honey mixture and fold in carefully.
4. Sift the bread flour into the egg mixture in stages, folding gently with a spatula to keep the volume.
5. Pour the batter into a loaf pan lined with parchment paper.
6. Bake in a preheated oven at 160°C for about 40 to 45 minutes until a toothpick inserted comes out clean.
7. Wrap the warm cake tightly in plastic wrap to lock in moisture and let it rest in the fridge overnight before slicing.


	





5. Mitarashi Dango - skewered, chewy rice dumplings grilled to add a smoky char and coated in a sweet soy sauce glaze. 
	Ingredients
	* Joshinko (rice flour) and Shiratamako (glutinous rice flour) mixed
* Warm water
* Soy sauce, mirin, and sugar (for the glaze)
* Potato starch (for thickening the glaze)
* Bamboo skewers


	Procedure
	1. Combine the rice flours and warm water, kneading gently until a smooth dough forms.
2. Roll the dough into small, uniform balls.
3. Boil the balls in water until they float, then cook for another 2 minutes before transferring to an ice bath.
4. Thread 3 to 4 dumplings onto each bamboo skewer.
5. In a saucepan, simmer soy sauce, mirin, sugar, water, and potato starch until a thick, clear, shiny glaze forms.
6. Quickly sear the skewered dumplings on a grill pan until slightly charred.
7. Brush the sweet soy glaze generously over the warm dango and serve.


	





6. Japanese Strawberry Shortcake - a light sponge cake layered with fresh strawberries and whipped cream, a staple for celebrations. 
	Ingredients
	* Sponge cake (flour, eggs, sugar, melted butter)
* Heavy whipping cream
* Powdered sugar
* Fresh strawberries (sliced)
* Simple sugar syrup
* 	Procedure
	1. Bake a standard sponge cake, let it cool completely, and slice horizontally into two even layers.
2. Whip the heavy cream and powdered sugar together until stiff peaks form.
3. Brush the bottom sponge cake layer lightly with simple sugar syrup to keep it moist.
4. Spread a layer of whipped cream over the sponge and arrange sliced strawberries evenly on top.
5. Apply more whipped cream over the strawberries, then place the second sponge layer on top.
6. Frost the entire top and sides of the cake smoothly with the remaining whipped cream.
7. Decorate the top with whole strawberries and chill before serving.


	





7. Taiyaki - a whimsical fish-shaped waffle cake crisp on the outside and packed with sweet custard or red bean paste. 
	Ingredients
	* Cake flour
* Baking powder
* Sugar and a pinch of salt
* Egg and milk
* Sweet vanilla custard or sweet red bean paste


	Procedure
	1. Whisk together flour, baking powder, sugar, and salt, then blend in the egg and milk until a smooth batter forms.
2. Preheat a taiyaki (fish-shaped) waffle iron over a medium-low flame and brush lightly with oil.
3. Pour batter into one side of the mold until it is half full.
4. Place a rectangular dollop of custard or red bean paste along the center of the fish mold.
5. Pour more batter on top to cover the filling completely.
6. Close the iron tightly and flip it immediately.
7. Cook for 2 to 3 minutes on each side until the exterior is a deep golden brown and crispy. Serve hot.


	





8. Coffee Jelly - a simple dessert consisting of cubes of black coffee gelatin served in a sweet, milky cream. 
	Ingredients
	* Strong brewed black coffee
* Gelatin powder
* Sugar
* Water
* Heavy cream or evaporated milk (for serving)


	Procedure
	1. Dissolve gelatin powder in a small bowl with a few tablespoons of warm water.
2. Mix hot, freshly brewed black coffee and sugar together in a pot until the sugar melts.
3. Stir the dissolved gelatin into the hot coffee mixture thoroughly.
4. Pour the mixture into a shallow rectangular dish.
5. Allow it to cool to room temperature, then place in the refrigerator for 3 hours until completely firm.
6. Slice the coffee gelatin into small cubes.
7. Divide cubes into glasses and pour heavy cream or sweet evaporated milk over them before serving cold.


	





9. Anmitsu - a traditional summer dessert bowl filled with agar jelly cubes, sweet toppings, and a dark sugar syrup. 
	Ingredients
	* Agar-agar powder (kanten)
* Water
* Sweet red bean paste (anko)
* Mochi pieces or dango
* Canned mixed fruits (mandarin oranges, cherries)
* Kuromitsu (Japanese black sugar syrup)
	Procedure
	1. Boil agar-agar powder and water in a pot for 2 minutes, pour into a container, and let it set into a firm jelly.
2. Cut the firm agar jelly into bite-sized cubes.
3. Arrange the jelly cubes at the bottom of a serving bowl.
4. Place a scoop of sweet red bean paste in the center.
5. Decorate the bowl around the red bean paste with the fruit pieces and chewy mochi.
6. Drizzle a generous amount of dark kuromitsu syrup over all the ingredients.
7. Serve chilled.
	





10.  Purin - a classic Japanese baked custard pudding with a silky smooth texture topped with a bitter-sweet caramel glaze. 
	Ingredients
	* Eggs
* Milk
* Sugar
* Vanilla extract
* Water (for caramel)
	Procedure
	1. Heat sugar and water in a saucepan over medium heat without stirring until it caramelizes into a dark brown syrup.
2. Pour the hot caramel immediately into the bottom of individual ramekin cups and let it harden.
3. Warm the milk and sugar in a pot until the sugar dissolves (do not boil).
4. Whisk eggs in a bowl, then slowly pour in the warm milk mixture while stirring constantly. Add vanilla extract.
5. Strain the custard liquid through a fine sieve into the caramel cups to ensure smoothness.
6. Place ramekins in a baking dish filled with hot water halfway up the sides.
7. Bake at 150°C for 35 to 40 minutes, cool down, chill, and unmold onto plates to serve.
	

JAPAN - BEVERAGES


1. Matcha Latte - a soothing, creamy green tea drink made from fine culinary matcha powder whisked into steaming hot milk. 
	Ingredients
	* Matcha powder
* Hot water
* Whole milk (or oat milk)
* Honey or sugar (optional)
	Procedure
	1. Sift the matcha powder into a bowl to remove any tiny lumps.
2. Pour a small amount of hot water (about 80°C) into the bowl.
3. Use a bamboo whisk (chasen) to whisk vigorously in a zig-zag motion until a frothy green layer forms.
4. Heat your milk and froth it slightly if desired.
5. Pour the warm milk into a serving cup.
6. Gently pour the whisked matcha tea on top of the milk.
7. Sweeten with honey or sugar if preferred and serve hot.
	



2. Genmaicha - a nutty and uniquely aromatic green tea blended with roasted popped brown rice grains. 
	Ingredients
	* Genmaicha loose tea leaves (green tea mixed with roasted brown rice)
* Hot water
	Procedure
	1. Place 1 to 2 tablespoons of genmaicha leaves into a Japanese teapot (kyusu).
2. Boil water and let it cool slightly to about 80°C to 85°C to avoid burning the green tea leaves.
3. Pour the hot water over the tea leaves in the teapot.
4. Close the lid and allow the tea to steep for exactly 30 seconds to 1 minute.
5. Pour the tea into cups in alternating small increments to distribute the flavor evenly.
6. Serve hot.
	



3. Hojicha - a earthy and deeply roasted green tea that has a reddish-brown color and a comforting, low-caffeine toasty flavor. 
	Ingredients
	* Hojicha tea leaves (roasted green tea)
* Boiling water
	Procedure
	1. Place hojicha tea leaves into a teapot.
2. Unlike regular green tea, boil water completely to 95°C to 100°C to extract the roasted aroma.
3. Pour the boiling water directly over the hojicha leaves.
4. Let the tea steep for about 30 seconds to a minute.
5. Pour completely out into tea cups so the remaining leaves don't become bitter.
6. Serve hot as a relaxing after-meal drink.
7. 	



4. Ramune - a fizzy, iconic Japanese carbonated soft drink traditionally sealed with a unique glass marble inside the bottle. 
	Ingredients
	* Store-bought Ramune soda bottle (original lemon-lime flavor) 
	Procedure
	1. Thoroughly chill the bottle of Ramune in the refrigerator before opening.
2. Peel off the plastic seal from the cap and remove the plastic plunger tool.
3. Place the bottle firmly on a flat, stable surface.
4. Position the plunger over the glass marble at the top of the bottle neck.
5. Push down hard with the palm of your hand until the marble pops down into the glass chamber below.
6. Hold down for a few seconds to prevent the carbonation from bubbling over, then drink cold.


	



5. Mugicha - a highly refreshing, caffeine-free roasted barley tea commonly served ice-cold during hot summer months. 
	Ingredients
	* Roasted barley tea bags (mugicha pack)
* Water
* Ice cubes
	Procedure
	1. Fill a large pitcher with 1 to 2 liters of cold tap or filtered water.
2. Drop a large mugicha cold-brew tea bag directly into the water.
3. Place the pitcher into the refrigerator.
4. Let it steep cold for 1 to 2 hours until the water turns a deep amber brown color.
5. Remove the tea bag from the pitcher to prevent the tea from turning bitter.
6. Pour into a glass packed with ice cubes and enjoy cold.


	

ASIAN - CHINA MAIN COURSE


1. Kung Pao Chicken - a classic Sichuan stir-fry featuring tender chicken cubes, crunchy peanuts, and spicy chili peppers. 
	Ingredients
	* Chicken breast or thighs (cubed)
* Roasted peanuts
* Dried red chili peppers
* Sichuan peppercorns
* Soy sauce, Chinese black vinegar, and sugar
* Garlic and ginger (minced)
* Scallions (green onions)
* Cornstarch (for velveted texture)


	Procedure
	1. Marinate chicken cubes with a bit of soy sauce and cornstarch for 15 minutes.
2. Mix soy sauce, black vinegar, sugar, and a splash of water in a bowl to make the sauce.
3. Heat oil in a wok and fry the dried chilies and Sichuan peppercorns until fragrant.
4. Add the marinated chicken and stir-fry until it turns white.
5. Toss in the minced garlic, ginger, and scallions.
6. Pour in the sauce mixture and stir quickly as it thickens.
7. Stir in the roasted peanuts and serve hot.


	



2. Mapo Tofu - a fiery, aromatic Sichuan dish of soft tofu set in a spicy, numbing minced meat sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Soft or silken tofu (cubed)
* Minced pork or beef
* Pixian Doubanjiang (chili bean paste)
* Gochugaru or Chinese chili flakes
* Ground Sichuan peppercorn powder
* Garlic and ginger (minced)
* Chicken broth or water
* Cornstarch slurry (for thickening)


	Procedure
	1. Blanch the tofu cubes in hot, salted water for 1 minute, then drain carefully.
2. Heat oil in a wok and fry the minced meat until crispy, then push to the side.
3. Add the chili bean paste, garlic, and ginger, stir-frying until the oil turns red.
4. Pour in the chicken broth and bring to a simmer.
5. Gently slide the tofu cubes into the sauce and simmer for 5 minutes.
6. Swirl in the cornstarch slurry to thicken the gravy.
7. Transfer to a bowl and dust heavily with ground Sichuan peppercorn powder before serving.


	



3. Sweet and Sour Pork - crispy fried pork nuggets tossed with bell peppers and pineapple in a vibrant tangy glaze. 
	Ingredients
	* Pork shoulder or tenderloin (cut into bite-sized pieces)
* Egg yolk and cornstarch (for battering)
* Bell peppers and onions (cut into chunks)
* Pineapple chunks
* Ketchup, rice vinegar, and sugar (for the sauce)
* Cooking oil for deep-frying


	Procedure
	1. Marinate the pork pieces with a splash of soy sauce, coat with egg yolk, and dread thoroughly in cornstarch.
2. Deep-fry the pork pieces until cooked through, then fry a second time at a higher heat for maximum crispiness.
3. In a clean wok, mix ketchup, vinegar, sugar, and a little water, heating until boiling.
4. Stir-fry the bell peppers, onions, and pineapple chunks in the sauce for 1 minute.
5. Toss the crispy fried pork quickly into the boiling sauce.
6. Coat every piece evenly and remove from heat immediately.
7. Serve hot while the pork is still crunchy.


	



4. Peking Duck - a world-famous imperial dish prized for its exceptionally thin, crispy skin and tender meat. 
	Ingredients
	* Whole duck
* Maltose syrup or honey mixed with water
* Five-spice powder
* Chinese thin pancakes
* Sweet bean sauce (Tianmianjiang) or Hoisin sauce
* Cucumber and scallions (cut into matchsticks)


	Procedure
	1. Clean the duck, pump air under the skin to separate it from the meat, and scald the skin with boiling water.
2. Brush the entire duck with the maltose syrup mixture and hang it to dry completely for several hours.
3. Roast the duck in an oven until the skin turns a shiny, deep mahogany brown and becomes crispy.
4. Carve the crispy skin and tender meat into thin slices.
5. To assemble, spread a smear of sweet bean sauce onto a thin pancake.
6. Place a few pieces of duck skin/meat, cucumber, and scallion matchsticks inside.
7. Roll tightly and enjoy.


	



5. Beef and Broccoli - a highly popular stir-fry featuring tender strips of beef and crisp broccoli florets in a rich brown sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Flank steak (thinly sliced against the grain)
* Broccoli florets
* Oyster sauce
* Soy sauce
* Minced garlic and ginger
* Shaoxing rice wine (optional)
* Cornstarch and baking soda (for tenderizing the beef)


	Procedure
	1. Marinate the beef slices with soy sauce, cornstarch, and a tiny pinch of baking soda for 20 minutes.
2. Blanch the broccoli florets in boiling water for 1 minute, then plunge into cold water to keep them bright green.
3. Heat oil in a wok over high heat and sear the beef slices quickly until browned but tender; remove from wok.
4. Sauté minced garlic and ginger in the remaining oil until fragrant.
5. Pour in oyster sauce, soy sauce, a splash of rice wine, and a bit of water.
6. Return the beef and the blanched broccoli to the wok, tossing rapidly to coat them in the bubbling brown sauce.
7. Serve hot with rice.


	



6. Wonton Noodle Soup - comforting egg noodles served in a clear broth along with delicate pork and shrimp dumplings. 
	Ingredients
	* Thin egg noodles
* Wonton wrappers
* Ground pork and minced shrimp (for filling)
* Sesame oil, white pepper, and soy sauce
* Chicken or pork bone broth
* Leafy greens (like bok choy)


	Procedure
	1. Mix ground pork, shrimp, soy sauce, sesame oil, and white pepper together to form the wonton filling.
2. Place a small spoonful of filling onto a wonton wrapper, fold, and pinch to seal securely.
3. Bring the seasoned chicken or pork bone broth to a gentle simmer in a pot.
4. In a separate pot of boiling water, cook the fresh egg noodles until al dente, then drain and transfer to a bowl.
5. Boil the wontons and leafy greens in the water until the wontons float and are cooked through.
6. Place the cooked wontons and greens neatly on top of the noodles.
7. Ladle the clear, piping-hot broth over the bowl and serve.


	



7. Yangzhou Fried Rice - a vibrant, aromatic rice dish tossed with an array of meats, shrimp, eggs, and scallions. 
	Ingredients
	* Leftover day-old cooked jasmine rice
* Chinese barbecue pork (Char Siu, diced)
* Small shrimp (peeled and deveined)
* Eggs (beaten)
* Green peas and diced carrots
* Scallions (finely chopped)
* Soy sauce or salt and white pepper


	Procedure
	1. Heat oil in a wok and soft-scramble the beaten eggs, then break them into small bits and set aside.
2. Stir-fry the diced carrots, peas, char siu pork, and shrimp until cooked.
3. Add the cold, day-old rice to the wok, breaking up any large clumps with the back of a spatula.
4. Stir-fry vigorously over high heat until the rice grains are hot and toasted.
5. Return the scrambled eggs to the wok and season with salt, white pepper, or a light splash of soy sauce.
6. Toss in the freshly chopped scallions during the last 30 seconds.
7. Serve hot.


	



8. Twice-Cooked Pork - a flavorful Sichuan classic where pork belly is first boiled, then sliced and stir-fried with leeks. 
	Ingredients
	* Pork belly chunk
* Sweet bean paste (Tianmianjiang)
* Chili bean paste (Doubanjiang)
* Chinese leeks or green bell peppers (sliced)
* Ginger and garlic (sliced)
* Shaoxing rice wine


	Procedure
	1. Boil the whole chunk of pork belly in water with ginger and rice wine for 20 minutes until parboiled; let it cool.
2. Slice the cooled pork belly into very thin, bite-sized strips.
3. Heat a wok over medium heat (no oil needed) and stir-fry the pork slices until they curl slightly and render their fat.
4. Push the pork to the side, then add the chili bean paste and sweet bean paste to the center, cooking until aromatic.
5. Mix the pork back into the sauce, tossing in the garlic, ginger, and sliced Chinese leeks.
6. Stir-fry quickly on high heat until the leeks are tender-crisp.
7. Serve hot.


	



9. Steamed Fish with Ginger and Scallions - a delicate Cantonese preparation that highlights the fresh, sweet flavor of whole fish. 
	Ingredients
	* Whole fresh white fish (such as sea bass or tilapia)
* Fresh ginger (finely julienned)
* Scallions (finely julienned)
* Light soy sauce, sugar, and water (for the seasoned soy sauce)
* Cooking oil


	Procedure
	1. Clean the fish thoroughly and make a few shallow diagonal cuts on both sides of the flesh.
2. Place the fish on a steaming plate, scattering a portion of the ginger slices on top and inside the cavity.
3. Steam over high heat for 8 to 10 minutes until the flesh flakes easily with a fork; discard any accumulated liquid.
4. Arrange a generous mound of fresh julienned scallions and remaining ginger on top of the hot fish.
5. Heat a few tablespoons of cooking oil in a small pan until smoking hot.
6. Carefully pour the hot oil directly over the scallions and ginger to sizzle and release their fragrance.
7. Pour a warm mixture of light soy sauce and a pinch of sugar around the base of the fish and serve.


	



10. Braised Pork Belly (Hong Shao Rou) - a popular Hunanese dish consisting of melt-in-your-mouth pork cubes glazed in a glossy, dark caramel sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Pork belly (cut into 1-inch cubes)
* Rock sugar
* Light soy sauce and dark soy sauce
* Shaoxing rice wine
* Star anise and cinnamon stick
* Ginger slices


	Procedure
	1. Blanch the pork belly cubes in boiling water for 3 minutes to remove impurities, then drain.
2. In a pot over low heat, melt rock sugar in a little oil until it turns into a golden-brown caramel syrup.
3. Add the pork cubes to the pot and stir quickly to coat them with the caramel.
4. Pour in the rice wine, light soy sauce, dark soy sauce, and enough water to submerge the meat.
5. Throw in the ginger slices, star anise, and cinnamon stick.
6. Bring to a boil, then cover and simmer on low heat for 1 hour until the pork is incredibly tender.
7. Uncover and crank up the heat to reduce the liquid into a thick, glossy glaze that clings to the pork. Serve hot.


	

CHINA - DESSERTS


1. Egg Tarts - a beloved dim sum pastry with a rich, silky egg custard baked inside a flaky, laminated crust. 
	Ingredients
	* Puff pastry or shortcrust pastry dough
* Egg yolks
* Evaporated milk or heavy cream
* Sugar
* Water
* Vanilla extract


	Procedure
	1. Dissolve sugar in warm water and let it cool completely.
2. Whisk egg yolks, evaporated milk, vanilla extract, and the cooled sugar water together.
3. Strain the liquid custard mixture through a fine sieve to ensure it is silky smooth.
4. Roll out the pastry dough and press into small tart molds.
5. Pour the egg custard mixture into the pastry shells until 80% full.
6. Bake in a preheated oven at 200°C (400°F) for 15 to 20 minutes until the crust is golden and the custard sets.
7. Serve warm.


	



2. Sesame Balls (Jian Dui) - crispy, deep-fried glutinous rice pastry coated in sesame seeds with a sweet red bean filling. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice flour
* Brown sugar dissolved in hot water
* Sweet red bean paste (anko)
* White sesame seeds
* Oil for deep frying


	Procedure
	1. Pour the hot sugar water into the glutinous rice flour and knead into a smooth, pliable dough.
2. Divide dough into small pieces, flatten, and wrap around a small ball of red bean paste, sealing completely.
3. Dampen the dough balls slightly with water, then roll them in white sesame seeds until fully coated.
4. Heat oil to a low temperature (around 150°C) and drop the balls in.
5. Fry while gently pressing down on the balls with a spatula to help them expand and become hollow.
6. Once they float and turn golden brown and crispy, drain excess oil.
7. Serve warm.
	



3. Mango Pomelo Sago - a refreshing, chilled dessert soup made of pureed mangoes, coconut milk, sago pearls, and tart pomelo shreds. 
	Ingredients
	Ripe sweet mangoes (cubed)
Sago pearls (tapioca pearls, cooked)
Pomelo or grapefruit segments (shredded)
Coconut milk
Evaporated milk or condensed milk


	Procedure
	Blend the majority of the mango cubes with coconut milk and evaporated milk until completely smooth.
Pour the mango puree into a large serving bowl.
Stir in the cooked, drained sago pearls.
Garnish the top generously with the remaining fresh mango cubes and shredded pomelo pulp.
Chill in the refrigerator for at least 2 hours.
Serve cold.


	



4. Red Bean Soup - a classic, warm dessert soup made from sweetened adzuki beans, often flavored with dried tangerine peel. 
	Ingredients
	* Dried red adzuki beans
* Rock sugar
* Water
* Dried tangerine peel (optional, for a citrus aroma)


	Procedure
	1. Soak the dried red beans in water overnight to soften.
2. Drain the beans and place them in a pot with fresh water and the dried tangerine peel.
3. Bring to a boil, then lower the heat, cover, and simmer for 1 to 1.5 hours until the beans are completely soft.
4. Use a wooden spoon to mash a portion of the beans against the side of the pot to thicken the soup texture.
5. Add rock sugar to taste and stir until completely melted.
6. Serve warm.


	



5. Tangyuan (Glutinous Rice Balls) - chewy rice balls stuffed with sweet black sesame paste, traditionally served in a warm ginger broth. 
	Ingredients
	* Glutinous rice flour and warm water
* Roasted black sesame powder
* Sugar and melted lard or butter (for filling)
* Water, rock sugar, and sliced ginger (for the broth)


	Procedure
	1. Mix black sesame powder, sugar, and melted butter together, then freeze until firm to make the filling.
2. Knead glutinous rice flour with warm water until a smooth dough forms.
3. Wrap small portions of the dough around cubes of the cold black sesame filling, rolling into smooth spheres.
4. In a separate pot, boil water with rock sugar and sliced ginger to make a sweet, warming broth.
5. Drop the rice balls into a separate pot of boiling water; cook until they float to the top.
6. Transfer the cooked balls into bowls and ladle the sweet ginger broth over them.
7. Serve hot.


	



6. Almond Tofu (Annin Tofu) - a delicate, jelly-like dessert flavored with sweet almond kernel milk, served chilled with fruit. 
	Ingredients
	* Almond extract or apricot kernel milk
* Agar-agar powder or gelatin
* Milk
* Sugar and water
* Canned fruit cocktail or mandarin oranges (for serving)


	Procedure
	1. Dissolve agar-agar powder in water and bring to a simmer for 2 minutes.
2. Stir in the milk, sugar, and almond extract until everything is fully incorporated.
3. Pour the mixture through a strainer into a flat dish.
4. Let it cool to room temperature, then refrigerate until firm and set.
5. Slice the almond jelly into neat diamond-shaped cubes.
6. Place cubes into a bowl, top with canned fruits and light syrup, and serve chilled.


	



7. Fa Gao (Fortune Cake) - a steamed sponge cake that splits into petal-like sections at the top, symbolizing prosperity. 
	Ingredients
	* All-purpose flour
* Rice flour
* Baking powder
* Brown sugar
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Dissolve the brown sugar completely in warm water and let it cool down.
2. Sift the all-purpose flour, rice flour, and baking powder together in a mixing bowl.
3. Pour the sugar water into the dry ingredients and whisk until a thick, smooth batter forms.
4. Pour the batter into small cups or molds lined with paper liners until almost completely full.
5. Bring a steamer to a rolling boil over high heat.
6. Place the cups into the steamer, cover tightly, and steam on high heat for 15 minutes without opening the lid.
7. Remove once the tops have cracked open wide into a "smile" and serve warm.


	



8. Deep-Fried Milk - an intriguing dessert with a hot, custardy, solidified milk center enclosed in a crunchy batter. 
	Ingredients
	* Milk
* Cornstarch and sugar (for the milk filling)
* Flour, baking powder, water, and oil (for the frying batter)


	Procedure
	1. Cook milk, sugar, and cornstarch in a pan over low heat, stirring continuously until it turns into a thick paste.
2. Pour the paste into a greased rectangular dish, smooth the surface, and freeze until completely solid.
3. Cut the frozen milk block into bite-sized rectangular sticks.
4. Whisk flour, baking powder, water, and a little oil together to make a smooth, thick frying batter.
5. Coat the frozen milk sticks thoroughly in the batter.
6. Deep-fry immediately in hot oil for 2 to 3 minutes until the shell turns golden and crispy while the inside melts.
7. Drain and serve immediately.


	



9. Snowflake Crisps - a modern, chewy, and crunchy treat made of melted marshmallows, biscuits, and dried fruits. 
	Ingredients
	* Marshmallows
* Butter
* Milk powder
* Hard milk biscuits (broken into pieces)
* Dried cranberries and chopped nuts


	Procedure
	1. Melt butter in a non-stick pan over very low heat.
2. Add the marshmallows and stir continuously until they are completely melted and smooth.
3. Turn off the heat and quickly stir in the milk powder until fully blended.
4. Throw in the biscuit pieces, dried cranberries, and chopped nuts, folding the sticky marshmallow mixture over them.
5. Transfer the warm mixture onto a piece of parchment paper and press it firmly into a thick square block.
6. Dust both sides generously with extra milk powder to resemble snow.
7. Allow to cool completely and become firm before slicing into neat little squares.


	



10. Sweet Osmanthus Jelly - a beautiful, translucent layered gelatin dessert embedded with fragrant dried osmanthus flower petals. 
	Ingredients
	* Dried osmanthus flowers
* Rock sugar
* Agar-agar powder or gelatin sheets
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Boil water with rock sugar until dissolved, then add the dried osmanthus flowers to steep for 5 minutes.
2. Stir agar-agar powder into the hot floral tea, cooking for another 2 minutes.
3. Pour a thin layer of the liquid into a mold and place it in the fridge briefly to partially set.
4. Stir the remaining liquid occasionally so the flowers don't all settle to the bottom.
5. Pour another layer over the first one once it's tacky to the touch.
6. Refrigerate the completed mold for 3 hours until completely firm.
7. Slice into translucent cubes and serve cold.


	

CHINA - BEVERAGES


1. Pearl Milk Tea (Boba) - the globally famous beverage combining rich black tea, milk, sweetener, and chewy tapioca pearls. 
	Ingredients
	* Black tea leaves (such as Assam or Ceylon)
* Whole milk or non-dairy creamer
* Cooked black tapioca pearls (boba)
* Brown sugar syrup or honey
* Ice cubes


	Procedure
	1. Brew a strong cup of black tea and let it cool down slightly.
2. Place a generous scoop of cooked tapioca pearls at the bottom of a tall glass.
3. Drizzle brown sugar syrup over the pearls to sweeten them.
4. In a shaker bottle, combine the brewed tea, milk, and ice, shaking vigorously.
5. Pour the milk tea mixture into the glass over the pearls.
6. Serve cold with a wide straw.


	



2. Chrysanthemum Tea - a light, golden herbal tea brewed from dried chrysanthemum flowers, enjoyed for its cooling properties. 
	Ingredients
	* Dried Chinese chrysanthemum flowers
* Rock sugar
* Hot water


	Procedure
	1. Place a handful of dried chrysanthemum flowers into a teapot.
2. Pour boiling hot water over the flowers.
3. Add rock sugar to the pot according to your preference.
4. Cover the teapot and let it steep for 5 minutes until the water turns a delicate yellow color.
5. Stir to ensure the rock sugar is fully dissolved.
6. Strain the tea into cups and serve hot (or let it cool and chill in the fridge for a refreshing iced tea).


	



3. Plum Juice (Suanmeitang) - a traditional, dark sweet-and-sour summer beverage made from smoked plums and hawthorn berries. 
	Ingredients
	* Smoked plums (Wumei)
* Dried hawthorn berries (Shanzha)
* Licorice root (Gancao)
* Rock sugar
* Water


	Procedure
	1. Rinse the smoked plums, hawthorn berries, and licorice root under running water.
2. Place all the herbs into a large pot with water and let them soak for 30 minutes.
3. Bring the pot to a boil, then turn down the heat and simmer gently for 40 minutes.
4. Stir in the rock sugar until completely dissolved.
5. Strain the dark liquid into a pitcher, discarding the solid ingredients.
6. Chill thoroughly in the refrigerator and serve cold, ideally during a spicy hot pot meal.


	



4. Cheese Tea - a modern tea trend featuring a base of cold brewed tea topped with a thick, savory-sweet layer of salted cream cheese. 
	Ingredients
	* Brewed green tea or Oolong tea (chilled)
* Cream cheese (softened)
* Heavy whipping cream
* Milk
* Sugar and a pinch of sea salt


	Procedure
	1. In a bowl, whip the softened cream cheese, milk, sugar, and sea salt together until smooth.
2. In a separate bowl, whip the heavy cream until it reaches soft peaks.
3. Gently fold the cream cheese mixture into the whipped cream to create a thick, velvety foam.
4. Fill a tall glass with ice cubes and pour the chilled green or oolong tea over them, leaving space at the top.
5. Carefully spoon the salted cream cheese foam on top of the tea so it floats in a thick layer.
6. Serve cold without a straw, drinking at an angle to taste both the cream and tea together.


	



5. Soy Milk (Doujiang) - a smooth, freshly blended beverage made from yellow soybeans, a quintessential Chinese breakfast staple. 
	Ingredients
	* Yellow soybeans
* Water
* Sugar (to taste)


	Procedure
	1. Soak the raw yellow soybeans in plenty of water overnight until they expand.
2. Drain and rinse the soaked beans.
3. Blend the beans with fresh water in a high-speed blender until completely smooth.
4. Pour the mixture through a nut milk bag or fine cheesecloth, squeezing hard to extract the milk and separate the pulp (okara).
5. Pour the raw soy milk into a pot and bring it to a boil over medium heat, stirring constantly so the bottom doesn't burn.
6. Let it simmer on low heat for 10 minutes to cook through safely.
7. Stir in sugar to taste and serve warm in a bowl or cup.


	

ASIAN - INDONESIA MAIN COURSE


1. Nasi Goreng - Indonesia's iconic fried rice dish, wonderfully aromatic and savory, seasoned with sweet soy sauce and spices. 
	Ingredients
	* Leftover cooked jasmine rice
* Sweet soy sauce (Kecap Manis)
* Chicken pieces and small shrimp
* Eggs
* Shallots and garlic (minced)
* Chili paste (Sambal)
* Cooking oil
* Fried shallots (for garnish)


	Procedure
	1. Heat oil in a wok and sauté the minced shallots, garlic, and chili paste until fragrant.
2. Add the chicken pieces and shrimp, stir-frying until cooked through.
3. Push the ingredients to the side, crack an egg into the wok, and scramble it.
4. Add the cold cooked rice to the wok, breaking up any clumps.
5. Pour in the sweet soy sauce and toss everything vigorously over high heat until the rice is evenly coated and toasted.
6. Season with a pinch of salt and pepper.
7. Serve hot, topped with fried shallots and a fried egg on the side.


	



2. Beef Rendang - a deeply flavorful, rich, and dry beef curry slow-cooked in coconut milk and a complex spice paste until melt-in-your-mouth tender. 
	Ingredients
	* Beef chuck or brisket (cut into chunks)
* Coconut milk and coconut cream
* Lemongrass, kaffir lime leaves, and turmeric leaves
* Toasted grated coconut (Kerisik)
* Spice paste (shallots, garlic, ginger, galangal, chili, coriander seeds)


	Procedure
	1. Blend the spice paste ingredients until smooth and place into a large, deep pot.
2. Add the beef chunks, coconut milk, lemongrass, and lime leaves into the pot, stirring well.
3. Bring the mixture to a boil over medium heat, stirring occasionally.
4. Lower the heat to a gentle simmer and let it cook uncovered for several hours until the liquid reduces drastically.
5. Stir in the toasted grated coconut (kerisik) to thicken and impart flavor.
6. Continue cooking and stirring frequently as the oil renders and the beef browns in its own fat.
7. Remove from heat when the dish is dark brown and almost dry, then serve.


	



3. Sate Ayam (Chicken Satay) - succulent skewered chicken thighs grilled over charcoal and drenched in a thick, savory peanut sauce. 
	Ingredients
	* Boneless chicken thighs (cubed)
* Coriander powder, turmeric powder, and sweet soy sauce (for marinade)
* Raw peanuts (fried and ground)
* Garlic, shallots, and candlenuts (for sauce base)
* Brown sugar and salt
* Bamboo skewers


	Procedure
	1. Marinate the chicken cubes in sweet soy sauce, coriander, turmeric, and oil for 1 hour.
